Chapter .xliii.
Of the incision of the abscess in the middle of the groin.
The ancients said this incision in the groin, and I have not seen any man in our land that it has been done.
And this is the inscription of the sermon of those.
But in men having a hernia, cover that the extraction of the groin be avoided, as for that it is not done well for its part because all the veins and major arteries of the body are here.
But in those who have abscesses caused in the mouth or groin or both ears, when the illness is not in the canal, cover that you use the incision of the groin to avoid the damage which is done by perforation.
Therefore, when we want this, that we incision the groin below three circles of the circles of the groin, or four with small incision for the latitude in that which is between two circles for quantity, that the incision be in ciph, not in the cartilage, and this place is convenient for incision, because it is deprived of flesh and the vessels of blood of it are there.
And if the doctor is fearful, cover that he extends the groin with an incision, and then fends the groin until it reaches the canal, but avoid the blood vessels if he sees any cause of them.
And then incision the ciph according to what we have recounted; and it is signified over the incision of the canal by the flame which is of that which is issued with that which is of its disruption and by the abscess of the voice.
And leave the wound open for some time.
Therefore, as the hour is remauguda in which perforation is feared, add two lips of the groin of the wound, and stitch that alone if it is the cartilage.
And then administer medicines that make flesh grow until it is healed.
And Albucasis says that the sum of the sermon which we have recounted, exposition is nothing but seeing that some of these abscesses have already opened the groin of the patient, and the patient has come into death, and the vein of it is cut off, and some go to incision the epiglottis so that the patient breathes over the place of the wound by some respiration, and be saved from death.
And for that, I command to leave the wound open until the malice of the illness is consumed; and the malice of it is for three days; and then command so the wound, and cure it until it is healed.
And what I have seen with my own eyes, is that a servant took a knife and placed it in her groin and incised with it a part of the canal of the lung, and I was called to the cure of her, and I returned the woman as if she was moaning of the dead, and I uncovered the wound and returned the blood which was issued from the wound small.
Therefore, I was confessed that she had not incised a vein nor guided it, and the wind was issuing from the wound, and I cured her until she was healed.
And I did not accuse the servant if not for the rawness in the voice, and after some days she returned to improvement of her dispositions.
And now I say that in the section of the epilepsy there is no fear.
Chapter XLIV.
Of the incision over the abscess which happens in the throat outside, and is called hernia of the throat.

Chapter XLV.
Of the incision of the species of nodes.
Of the nodes there are many species and I have already said all the species of them in the division.
And I want to count as the difference between a node and an excrescence as if making a doubt.
Therefore, I say that in an excrescence there is heat and fever and vehement pain until the boiling of the superfluity is appeased; and it is complicated putrefaction that at that hour ceases the fever, the pain, and the heat.
But in a node there is no heat nor fever nor pain, and it counts that which is like a lion's mane that is in the sac proper.
And it is according to the color of the body, and the beginning of it is like a bulb and is made like a vase, whether it is larger or smaller, and they are according to two species, whether they are fatty and contain humidity, and the colors of the humidity are many, according to what I said in the division.
Therefore, when you come to the cure of a node, that you examine it and inquire about it at the beginning with the instrument that is called intromes, according to how it will come its form in the chapter which is close to this.
And the manner of inquiry of abscesses and of all nodes, and it is that you take this instrument and introduce it into the place most humid which you find in the abscess, and you revolve your fingers with it little by little until you know that the instrument has already penetrated the core.
And then lastly your hand according to the measure of the greatness of the abscess, and then you extract the intromes and consider what is issued in the trace of it.
And if the humidity is flowing out, of whatever color it may be, then you incise it with a superficial incision according to what I have said in the other abscesses.
And if from the trace of the intromes there is no humidity, then you know that it is fatty.
And dry over it with an incision having the shape of a cross according to this shape: as I have taught you, and suspend that with forceps, and exfoliate the core from all parts with ease, and guard the skin or sac, if you can, over it and extract that sania with the node.
But if it is broken in the operation, it is not possible to extract that sania, and many times it must be done, and then you extract it in pieces until nothing of it remains.
Because if from it remains nothing, little or much, the node returns according to the most.
And if you see that from it remains some small part, then complete the wound with some corrosive powders sharp and strengthen the wound, and place over that which sits abscess caut, and cure that of the other cure until it is healed.
And if it is a large node, then you sew the two lips of it and cure that with what is necessary for healing.
But if a pulsatile vein is opposite it, or non-pulsatile, then you cut and moisten the place with three times-distilled vitriol and leave that straight for two or three days until you can scar the wound and that the boiling of the blood is appeased; and then return to incise what is remaining of the node.

Chapter .xlix.
Of the incision of abscesses that occur because of an artery or vein.
When an artery is broken, and the tissue that is above it is consolidated, then many times an abscess occurs. And the signs by which it is known that inflammation and abscess are due to the artery or vein: because when an abscess is due to an artery, it is long aggregated in the front of the body; and that when you pierce the abscess with your fingers, you feel in it a kind of stridor.
And that one which is due to a vein is round and prominent on the body.
And the incision on this abscess is an error, and most of all in the one that is under the armpits, and in the angles, and in the neck, and in many places of the body; and it is very large, therefore, that its cure with iron should be avoided, and the one that is in the extremities, or in the head, should be avoided.
But on the one that is of them because of the inflammation of the orifice of the artery, cut in the tissue a long incision; and then open the incision with probes and the artery, and delirate the tunics until it is uncovered.
And then put on that needle and make it penetrate into the other side, and tighten the artery with a double thread in two places, — which causes you to be able to extract two arteries which are in the temples.
And then prick the place which is between two ligaments with a spatula until the blood that is in it comes out, and the abscess is dissolved.
And then administer a cure in which is generated power until the ligaments fall; and then take care of it with suitable ointments until it is healed.
And if the abscess is due to a section of a vein, then you should have with your hand that which is possible of the abscess with the tissue, and then introduce the needle under the place which you have had under your hand, and make it penetrate; and be in that double thread until you extract it from the other side, and then ligate the abscess with a good ligament according to what I have told you in the ligament of the grape of two parts with two extremities of the thread.
But if you fear that the thread will be extracted, then introduce the thread with that needle under the entire abscess, after the incision of the first needle, and tighten your threads in four places.
Then dry the abscess in the middle of it until when it is extracted that which is in it, then you should cut the superfluity of the tissue, and leave that which is tied from it.
And then place on it the powder which you have soaked in wine and oil, and then administer the cure which is made with herbs and ointments while it is healing.
Chapter 1 of the abscess which occurs due to twisting of nerves.
Thus as abscesses occur in arteries and veins, and similarly abscesses occur in nerves when they are struck or occur due to excessive labor, and similarly.
And it is made most in the places of the arms or the ankle, or in any place where the joints are ill.
And it is a serious abscess, and it is similar in color to the rest of the body, and in the majority of its dispositions, it is surrounded by them and when it is squeezed with violence, the patient feels like a stupor.
And it is not an abscess that is added in the front of the body, and for this reason, the code is left, and it is ill in all parts and does not go to the parts in front or behind.
Therefore, those that are in the joints should not be enclosed with iron, because it will become very dangerous contraction.
But that which is in the head or on the forehead, close the wound with a spatula. But if it is a small abscess, then take it with the forceps and cut it from the root.
And if it is large, then suspend it with a hook, and scrape it, and then cover it; and adjust the wound with sutures, and care for it until it is healed.
Chapter 2.
Of the incision of the abscess which occurs from the cheek that occurs to the belly.
And it happens to some men, growths appear in the bellies of those and in the other parts of the body of those, which are called fungous because of their similarity to fungi, of which the root is subtle and the head of it is thick; and already the lips of those are turned, and it is of those that is small, and it is of those that is greatly magnified.
And I have already seen one, and in the belly of him there were two parts which were more like fungi, and there was no difference between those white, of fine root.

Chapter .lxix.
Of castration.
Know that castration in our law is forbidden, but for a reason it is written to me that I remember it in this book; and it is not necessary to remember it except for two ways, of which one is that it be in the knowledge of the physician when he is asked about it, that he knows the cure of it to whom it happens; and the other way is that we have many times need of castration of other animals for our benefit, such as of many, and of goats, and of pigs, and of those similar to the animals.
And therefore I say that castration is done in two ways: either by attrition, or by fissure to section.
But in that which is done by attrition, the way of the operation is that we make the beast to be submerged in warm water until its genitals are softened and are limp and hanging. And then take them with your hand until they are soft and do not appear after the touch.
But in castration done by fissure and section, when you have the beast and press the scrotum of it with your left hand.
And then lie the suspensory, and cut over each wound with a section between two wounds processed.
And then cut those that you will have each excoriated. And do not let on those of the cloth any cause, but the thin cloth which is over the veins.
And this way of castration is better the one done by attrition, because attrition firmly leaves no cause of the testicles for which the beast desires coyt.
And then cure the wound until it is healed.

And if they are difficult, some of them, in childbirth, and they come to what we have said of unnatural figures, then you care for them as we have recounted.

Remembrance of what is formed in the womb from embryos and miscarriages.
Sometimes they are formed in the womb, one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, and sometimes ten, and it has already been verified that one woman aborted six, and another gave birth to ten, the cause of which was made by the measurement of the glorious wise men.
And all this covers what should be in the science of the midwife, for great learning is given to that person who seems to resemble this, and therefore, pause is given to that as it should be.

Of the extraction of the fetus when it is dead.
When you cure the dead fetus with what we have said in the division of the medicine, and it is not born outside, and you are forced to use the operation with your hand, then you should consider if the woman is of sound virtue and is not with any of the accidents by which she is feared for destruction.
Then you should place the woman on her back on the bed, and her head should be inclined downwards, and her legs should be elevated.
And the minister should have those of two parts, or be tied on the bed so that the body of him does not extend during the extraction of the fetus.
And then you moisten the mouth of the mother with humid oils and with a mucilage of althea and fenugreek and the seed of lily.
And then the midwife anoints her hand with those oils and mucilages, and then she introduces her hand with facility into the mother, and then she seeks with the hand the place in which the hooks will be in the fetus.
And convenient places in this: therefore, you consider if the fetus is prepared that it descends upon its head, and then you place the hooks in its heels, or in the neck, or in the mouth, or in the palate, or below the beard, or in the fork of it, or in the proper places of the back, or below the hypochondria.
But if the descent is on the feet of it, then in the penile, or in the middle of the back.
And you should have the hook with your right hand, and pause the curvature of it in that place which is between the fingers of your left hand, and introduce your hand with facility and place the hook in one of those places which we have said, until you arrive at the left cause.
And then pause and place in the position of it another hook, or the third if it is necessary, so that the traction is equal, and not an extension according to its rectitude alone.
And be careful to every part, so that the movement of it is alleviated as it is done during the eradication of it.
And be sure in it that which is between them, the extension is softened; and if any part of it is retained, then the midwife anoints some of her fingers with oil and introduces them skillfully and revolves with those that are retained.
Therefore, if the part of the fetus is born, then the hooks should be changed into the place which is more outward; and do so until the whole fetus is born.
But if the hand is outside the other, and it is not possible to reduce it by the constriction of it, then the midwife should wrap a cloth over it; and then extract it until the whole is born, and incise it either at the junction of the hand or in the groin.
And so you should do in the other hand and in the two feet.
But if the head of the fetus is large, or there is an accident to it constriction in the movement, or there is water adjusted in the head of it, then the midwife should introduce between the fingers the spatula spines and fenda the head and extract the water, or that which disfigures it with an instrument which is named "alundat", the form of which will come with the forms of the other instruments in the chapter which is next.
And similarly, if the bone is broken in a large place by nature, and then the bone is inserted into the flesh, or the bone is nourished as we have said; then extract the bones with forceps.
And if the head is broken and is constricted by the collarbone, then it is cut so that the moisture which is in the feet is poured out.
But if it is not complicated, nor does it obey easily, then you cut the head as much as is possible to you.
And if the bowels of the belly are festering or are in it hydrophic, then you must pierce it so that the moisture which is in it runs out.
But if the matter is on their feet, then the traction of it is lighter and the direction of it to the mouth of the mother is lighter.
But if it is constricted by the belly and the foot, then you must extract that cloth which you will have enveloped over your hand, and that you cut the belly and the foot so that the water which is in those runs out.
But if the other members are stayed and the head returns, then the metron inserts her left hand; but if the mouth of the mother is open, then she inserts her hand into the preon of the lair, and searches with that the head, and pulls that into the mouth of the mother, and then inserts into it a hook, or two hooks, and pulls it with those.
And if the mouth of the mother is constricted by an abscess caused by a boil, then it is necessary that it not be troubled over it; but you must administer an infusion of moist, fatty causes. And administer plasters; and follow the patient in waters that soften and moisten.
And if the matter is on their side, then if possible, it should be lanced; and it should be administered with the water we have said in the living matter.
And if that is not possible, then it should be incised in pieces, and extracted.
And you must leave no cause of the second kind.
And when you have completed your entire operation, then administer the water we have said of the cure for the abscesses caused by the mother.
And if there occurs a flow of blood, then descend into astringent waters and administer the other cure.
And I have already seen a woman in the belly of whom a child was dead, and then above that fire another pregnancy, and then the dead child is another. It happened to me a long time ago an abscess in his navel; and it inflated so that it was open, and it began to throw out pus.
And I was called to the cure of him, and medicated him for a long time, and the plague did not consolidate.
Then I placed upon him some causes of plaster of strong traction, and extracted from him a bone, and after passing some days, and extracted another bone; and I was too amazed, as in the belly there were no bones.
And then I thought that they were of the bones of the dead fetus.
Therefore I continued to investigate the plague, and extracted from it more bones, the woman existing in her thousands of dispositions, and already living in such a manner for a long time, correcting of it a little of pus.
And I do not affirm that it is strange, but that in this there is science and help to what the physician artificially administers with his hand for cure.
Of the forms of the instruments that are necessary to extract the fetus.
Form of the verge with which the mother is opened:
This is the form of the stretcher in which the free ends are fastened, to which fastening there are two verges in two extremities of two feet. But however this verge must be more subtle of stricter, and be made either of ebony or of wood of boys.
And it should be the width of each rod two fingers and the margin of each one is one finger, and the length of each one is a palm and a half; and in the middle place of the two rods are two adjustments of that same half rods, of which the length is the majority of a palm and a little more, and the width of each one is two fingers, or a little less.
And these two addaments are inserted into the mouth of the mother so that it may be opened with those when you revolve the two prescribed verges.
Another form similar to that more subtle and lighter:
It is made of ebony or wood rods according to the resemblance of forceps. But however at the extremity of it there are two addaments as it were, and the length of those addaments is about a palm, and the width of each one is two fingers.
And as you want with those to open the mother, then you make the woman lie on the sheet with her feet hanging, open that which is between her thighs. And then open your hand with the instrument as you do with forceps, similarly according to the quantity that you want of the opening of the mouth of the mother until the metron makes it as you want.

Of extraction of the secondine.
When the secondine is retained during childbirth, then you command the patient to retain her breath, and then make that stirnuation with condition, and strengthen your hand over the mouth of her and over her nostrils, and if by this it is outside, it is good.
And if not, then you take a bowl and perforate in the cover a hole and place in that herbs inside the mouth of the mother, like calamint and rue and anise and chamomile and sicados arabic and cinnamon and centaury. All these herbs or some of them are submerged in water in the bowl, and place that over the fire.
And then place a canula of cane in the mouth of the mother, and hold that inside until the vapor comes to the cavity of the mother.
And then make that stirnuation as we have said, and the secondine is thrown out with speed.
But if this cure remains and it is not thrown out, then you command the midwife to submerge her left hand in sesame oil or in a mixture of althea, and then introduce that into the conh and caress with that the secondine, and as that has been found, then take it and extend it little by little. But if it is annexed in the preon of the mother, then introduce her hand as we have recommended, and when she has found the secondine, extract it little by little according to the rectum so that the mother does not feel the traction vehemently. And be careful that it be changed to the right and left sides with facility.
And if the mouth of the mother is constricted, we have already recommended the cure with stirnuation and with the medication of the bowl with herbs.
But if it is not thrown out with all the causes that we have recommended, then guard yourself that you do not fatigue yourself over that in iteration of abstraction, but rather that what is emitted from it to the mouth of the mother lies to the cloyssa of the woman, and then sterilize that with enguent and tetrafarmacon; because that will make it rot then after a few days and it will be dissolved and it will be thrown out.
But when you can, it is elevated from it bad odor to the head, and to the stomach, and that you read the patient; and therefore it should be administered sub-fumiguacios and convenient to that.
But some of the Ancients already are esproatz sub-fumigation of nazitort and of dried figs.
Form of instrument with which the woman is sub-fumigated ofves the retention of menstruation and of the secondine:
It is made of veyre or of eram.
And it is placed the subtle extremity in the conh and the wide extremity over the fire, and the sub-fumigation is placed over the embers of the fire.
And hold that inside until that sub-fumigation is consumed and iterate another.
Of cure of the unperforated child's bottom.
Many children are born and the bottoms of them are not perforated, the ones that already have a subtle and opilated ciphac. Therefore it behooves the midwife to perforate with her said that ciphac; and if not, perforate that with a sharp spatum, and guard yourself that it does not touch the lacert.
And then place on that wool infused in wine and oil; and then cure that with enguent inside until it is senat.
But if you fear that it is opilated, then place in the trauc a canula for many days, and remove it when the child will want to degir.
And already accideys oppilacio of the bottom by consolidation of plague or of apostema; therefore it behooves that that consolidation be incised, and then be cured with that which we have said of the cure and of the lead.
Of the cure of fistulas that have opened.
Fistulas that have opened in the parting of the buttocks, low with discharge and thickness, which have opened near the anus or in the space between the buttocks.
And it is a fistula or a multitude of fistulas.
And as that nodularity is ancient and runs with the moisture of white, viscous, or subtle pus, and sometimes from these fistulas some penetrate.
And those that penetrate are known by what is emitted from them by the outflow and by the windiness; and sometimes the patient feels the outflow, and very often it is emitted from them worms.
And sometimes from these fistulas some penetrate into the space into the bladder, and into the meat of the vagina; and some penetrate into the junction of the thigh and into the knot of the groin.
And in which it is known that a fistula penetrates into the anus and does not penetrate, it is that you put your finger inside the anus, and you enter a subtle probe of thread or iron into the fistula when there is no turgescence.
But if there is turgescence, then enter into that a subtle probe of lead or of horsehair until you feel the probe or the hair in your finger.
And if you do not feel that at all, nor does it proceed from the tract any cause of evacuation or worms or windiness, thus as we have said, then know that it is non-penetrating, and then turn to the cure.
And when the fistula is penetrating into the bladder or into the meat of the vagina, then the signification of it is the emission of urine from that and prohibition of it as that the place may be consolidated with medicine.
But if it is penetrating into the junction of the thigh or into the groin and causing pain in the circuit, then the sign of it is that the probe enters here if there is no turgescence into the groin, and causing pain in the circuit of the parting; and that from it there is pus always; and that it is not of value in that medicine, nor is it consolidated with an enema.
And in all those penetrating fistulas there is no cure of all, and the cure of those is the work and vanity of the physicians upon which it is founded.
But in that which is not penetrating and not ancient, healing with iron is expected according to what I have told you, and what I have already proved.
And it is that the patient lies between your hands on their two, and raises their legs into them, the thighs being inclined to their belly, and then enter a probe of lead, or of thread if there is turgescence in the fistula, until you know the place where the probe enters.
And if that feels the patient around the buttock, then cover that you enter your finger inside the buttock.
And if you feel in your finger the probe already by itself enters uncovered, or another that you feel between your finger and that skin or flesh, then you know certainly that that is penetrating; and therefore do not work on that, because it is not in that healing, as we have said.
But however, some say that it is healed in some men tart.
And of the medicine by which healing is expected in it is that you ignite a subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as it is preceded, and enter that ignited into the fistula until it reaches around the buttock; and then repeat that twice or three times until you know that all those flesh adjusted to the fistula have been seared, which are similar to the feather quill of a bird.
And then cure that with poultices wrapped in border until they can all those flesh that are seared, and then cure that with medicines the flesh generating and consolidating, and if it is healed, good is; and if not, then it is not healed in any time by other cure.
And if the probe enters, and does not penetrate into your finger which is in the buttock, and between that and the probe which is veiled with flesh or skin, and sometimes the fistula in that which seizes the surface of the pudendum, then dry the pudendum from the beginning of the fistula, and you see drying by the probe, and it is in the fistula until the drying reaches the place in which the extremity of the probe reaches, and by the probe it is liberated and catched.
And then purify those fistula flesh which are assembled to the feather quill of a bird and do not remain any cause from those.
But if a flux of blood sometimes comes between you and your operation when you are cauterizing those flesh, then the best that is and of the lighter instrument is to cauterize with fire or with acute medicine, because cauterizing with fire adjusts good twice habits: it is the searing of those flesh adjusted, and abscessing of the blood excretion of the humidities.
And then cure that with poultices wrapped in border or in a caus trissat until the place gets braced, and then cure the plague with enemas of hard flesh generating and consolidating.
And so medicines in which there is stypticity and excretion; when then it is restored already healed and you fear no iteration.
But if the fistula already reaches into the preon of the buttock and is elongated from that to the surface of the body, then enter your finger into the buttock and inquire with that.
And therefore if you feel the tension and between you and her is a veil of cloth or flesh, and it is ready for penetration, then it is not an operation on her, but according to your trust and hope.
This cause is administered in her in three ways: or that you cauterize her as we have said; or that you succeed her inside while you obtain the cavity of her so that it is possible for you to introduce the instruments and the proper cure; and do not process it with a section so that you do not cut the ligament containing the tail, and that it occurs on the patient as an effect of the will of the spirit; and then cure her with what we have said, which is a strong and safe healing; or that you lengthen that veil and cleanse that pus that dries her inside towards the anus, as we have said, or with a probe or another instrument of sharp extremity, and then cleanse those fistulous flesh that are in the section inside where you can make a percuction; and then strive to make the restoration of the whole wound with a section, and if the pus orifice above is not consolidated, and the fistula remains open in the part of the anus, and pus is light for the patient. And sometimes the fistula is finished in this way: it is when you introduce the probe into the fistula, and it is in the place of the anus around the surface of the body with the tendon and on the edge of the anus, then take a probe of perforated extremity, which is like a needle for preparing the hearts according to this form:
And introduce it into that faithful envelope of v threads or around them; and then introduce the probe with a thread into the fistula until you obtain its cavity.
But if it is penetrating in the edge of the anus towards the inside, then you extract the thread from that tract so that you introduce your finger into the anus; and extract the extremity of the thread and adjust the two extremities simultaneously, and tighten each one, and leave it for a day or two, and when you see the thread more deeply inserted into the flesh, tighten well that inside so that those flesh that are between the two extremities of the thread and that close.
And then cure the wound until it is consolidated and healed.
But if the orifice of the fistula is not penetrating, then make it penetrate, in whatever way it is prepared for you, but not in the preon, because it is not you who should do this so that you do not cut the ligament; and then make it with that inside so that it is healed.
The form of the spatum spinos with which the fistula is fended: the curvature of which is very sharp and the other part is blunt, so that you do not cut what is not necessary, as sometimes.
Of suturing hemorrhoids in which blood runs in the incision of those.
Hemorrhoids are in two ways, because they are between the anus resembling this way that they are of carbs, or that those are like the fat of rasim. And of those are small and large, and that the blood runs from those always and is one, and are many, and are outside the anus, and in the extremities of it.
But however those that are outside the anus are according to the less humidity, of which runs a little yellow water or a little blood with continuous body, and are according to the color of the body.
And the cure of that which is inside the anus is that you command the patient to squat and to express himself until the anus is empty and the hemorrhoids appear to you. Then you take and suspend with hooks or what you have those with your fingernail, and then cut those deeply their roots.
But if the hooks are not held in those by the humidity of them and their softening, then take those with rough cloth or with a stick or with a wool fleece, and extract those with your fingers, and then cut those and pulverize over them some powders caudas near the incision, so that they are applied to those in place of cauterization; or cauterize those according to what is preceded in the chapter of cauterization. And then cure those with the other cure until they are healed.
And if the anus does not obey the egress, then christenize the patient with a christer in which is a small bite, and wash it with that water that is in the anus and that obeys the egress lightly when the patient expresses himself.
But if the hemorrhoids are outside the anus, then the cause of them is lighter, and it is that you take those with your fingernail, or that you take those with a hook, and cut those, and then cure those with the water that we have said until they are healed.
And that one who has an incision, cover that you administer suture of them according to this way: take thread enveloped and introduce it into a needle and then extract the hemorrhoids to the upper parts, and make that penetrate with the needle in the root of the other part, and envelop the two extremities of the thread in the part below the needle, and it is longitudinally; and tighten the hemorrhoid with a strong structure, and then untie the thread and extract the needle.
And do this to all, and leave one of them untied, so that the superfluity of the blood runs from that one.
And then place on the anus cloth infused in rose oil or in cerot; and place that over the anus and command the patient to rest. And then leave that one inside that box; and when it is closed, cure those with ointments or another cure inside that box.
And since they are old and do not heal in that medicine, then when you cut those with the point of a spatula or with your nail until they are made moist and the discharge of pus from them is hosted, which prohibits them from consolidating; and then cure those when they are consolidated.
Then you must open those with a strong pus that the first one when it is blood and is excoriated; and then cure those when they are healed.
Know that alamermar, it is clear, and it is not if not a red spot according to the color of the body resembling a keyhole, and it is made in the whole body and mostly in the parts below the feet and the knees, and therefore by those pains you must know the ailment.
And therefore, when it is incised that which is in the circuit of the key, and it is held with the forceps or a pincer, and it is eradicated from its root; and then cure that.
And if you wish, cauterize the following as it is preceded in its chapter.
But of warts is a small, rough, fistulous, round eminence on the surface of the body, and many times they come in the most of the children.
And the cure of it is that you extend and cut that, or that you tighten that with a thread or a needle inside that box. And if you wish, cauterize that, as we have said, with fire or with acute medicine.
But a formica is a small eminence, feutrada or fistulous, thick on the surface of the body going into the preon, and when the  freg finds that it is felt in it resembling a bite of an ant, and it is made around the body.

Sometimes christening is done of silver or of laton or of iron melted or malleated; and sometimes it is done of those instruments small and large according to those to whom they are administered, that that which is administered in the cure of the little children be small; and of those whose buttocks are raw or sore, the christenings of those be small.

And if the medicine forces him to vomit, he should have as much as he can; and if he sleeps with it all night, he is more likely to recover.

Of the cure of plagues.
And I have already said in the division of the cure of plagues what was convenient to the free, and I say so the cure of those with my hand and with medicines according to the complement.
Therefore, I say that plagues are diversified according to what they are made of and according to the place on which they fall.
And the causes by which many times plagues are made are such as a bite of a snake, or an incision of a sword or spear, or a blow with a lance, or a club, or an arrow, or similar to those of many causes.
But the plagues that are in the places of the body are such as a plague which falls on the head, or the neck, or the feet, or the belly, or the arm, and similar to those of the limbs.
And I am recounting the cure of some plagues so that you pause that reasoning and rule over the others.
And I will begin with the plagues of the head, for the remembrance of the composed ones will come at the beginning of the third chapter.
Therefore, I say that when a simple plague occurs in the head and it is not a fracture, then consider: if it is from a snakebite or similar, and the wound has already been cleansed alone and it is a large plague and you fear an abscess forming on that patient's head, then you should cauterize and perform cephalic flebotomy immediately, and do not delay this; and extract from that blood according to the quantity of its virtue, if no other cause prohibits flebotomy, especially if the blood that is extracted from the plague is little.
And let the flebotomy be on the opposite side of the afflicted area; and guard the patient from repletion and from wine and from heavy foods.
But if from the ministration any cause prohibits, then let the food be lessened and do not approach meat nor wine.
And place on the plague, if an abscess forms, cauterize, and infuse into it olive oil roasted alone or into wine in which is steeped.
But if it is certain of an abscess cauterize, then place on the plague, if it is recent and the air has not changed that, the powder which I will recount a little later.
And if the air has already changed that, then place on alum, until it is healed.
But if the plague is large or is from an incision of a sword and similar, and the lips of it are not adjusted by puss, then adjust those with suture according to how I will recount of the suture of them.
But if the plague is already discovered from the bone and skin, and it is not a retention of it but a small suspension, then incise that and then cure the plague with medicines and restore the flesh in the place of the wound, and command the patient to be careful of foods in which there is greasiness: caps and form cooked meat and similar to them, until it is composed.
And if a putrefaction occurs in the wound and it does not adhere to the bone, then you incise all that pus and throw it out, and then cure that.
But if in these plagues an artery or vein is found from which blood can flow, and it is not severed by medicines, then you inquire about the artery, and if you find that un-incised, then you incise that with a spatula, or cut it; and if necessity provokes that what we have said does not confer, then you cauterize until the blood is severed.
And if these plagues are simple and small, then the cause of them is lighter;  in this way that you pulverize on those this powder, for it consolidates before the air changes them.
And the manner of the powder is this: take olive oil, one part, dragon's blood, two parts, and non-extinct cautery, three parts; be all three ground and sifted, and from it, fill the plague, and be it constricted by good constriction until it well adheres on that, and be coagulated with blood.
And then strengthen that with poultices and leave it, and do not untie it while it is like this so that it is not apostemed, for no medicine is extracted from it until it is healed.
And sometimes do this solely cauterize, when it is not to you in present olive oil and dragon's blood.
And already do this same operation in the great plagues when it is necessary that it be laid upon them and be constricted, and are recent plagues with their blood, those which the air has not altered.
And if the air has altered them, and especially when it is in summertime, then it is not understood in the position of this powder, but rather cure those with what we have said, in this way that you place on those some digested unguents, or that you place on those dust of barley flour with water and honey until they get a poultice; and then cure those with the other cure until they are healed.
But if it happens to the plague fracture in bones, and it is small, then you extract it with a tool.
And I will say the cure for fractures of the head in that which is poisonous.
Of the plagues of the neck.
But if the plague happens in the neck, then there is no difference in medication, and between the plague of the head when it is simple.
But if already the nerve of the neck is cut or artery, then if it is a nerve, it is not in its place but that its cure be avoided with that which makes vehement clotting, such as zinc and zeger that is vitriol and similar to their quills no to the nerves and against that. And do not place on the plague any cause of all cold, because the substance of the nerves is cold and the continuation of it is with the brain, which is the most important of all the members.
And if that is cured with light medicines, such as it is washed with sweet water, some herbs infused in rose or non-rose oil, and then washed with sweet water and the other pebbles minced in this manner, and moistened.

And because he despaired of me, he returned to his land and I came to know that the man prepared and incised his hand entirely, and he was healed.
And I have not added this narration except so that it may be an aid on what catches of this malady, and that its significance for which it is signified and according to which it is worked.
Of the cure of the intestines and the quality of clysterization with medicines.
When abscesses happen in certain fleshy members and the space of the abscess is prolonged until it makes a collection of pus, and then it is broken and perforated, and pus is ejected from it, and the place remains empty as if it were a vessel, and the skin that is above it is as delicate cloth, and it has not reached posterior corruption, and it has not imprinted on the bone or on the nerve or on the ligament, it is called a sinus, and it is not named a fistula.
But however, if the space is prolonged until the corruption presses on some member, then it is called a fistula and not a sinus.
And the cure of it is that the skin is incised entirely as it is revolved, and mostly when it is delicate and is made like cloth, and comfizas that it does not adhere to the place by its corruption.
But if you hope that the skin adheres and that that corruption has not achieved posterior consequence, and in the skin there has passed through from the front, then you cure that with clysters.
And it is that you consider the sinus, and then if it is large, and the brac that you see is of fetid odor, then you clysterize that with Egyptian medicine, which is of oil and strong wine and zinc receiving equal parts, and they are put in a vessel, and they are boiled over the fire until the medicine becomes thick and reaches the consistency of honey.
And then you take from it what is necessary and dissolve it with water and honey; and clysterize with that the sinus, and strengthen the orifice of it, and leave the medicine in it for the quantity of two hours.
And then extract that with care; and do this for so many days until the sinus is purified and the stench is removed.
And sometimes it is clysterized with ash water, when the medicine is not present to you; and it is that you take the ash of wheat, and put water over it; and then you collect that and clysterize with it until you confess that the sinus is then healed.
And if the patient does not tolerate the Egyptian medicine nor the ash water, then clysterize with water and honey and that it be mixed with crushed zinc, and clysterize with wine and honey mixed, for by the property of honey is that it purifies and washes, and wine makes the sinus adhere, and especially when in the wine there is superfluity of astringency and dryness.
And as you do this sometimes and you confess that the sinus is already healed, then clysterize with water that makes flesh grow in it.
And it is that you take of dyphtheritic ointment and dissolve it with rose oil and astringent wine; or that you clysterize with some medicines and other ointments that have the properties of which I have already written in the treatise of the ointments.
And if the orifice of the sinus is narrow in which the clyster nozzle is not received, then you enlarge it with a small iron little by little, and place in it a poultice wrapped in Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it is enlarged.
And similarly if the orifice is wide, then you add the lips of it with suture and leave of it the quantity in which between the clyster its addition.
And if the patient's orifice from which the arm comes out is elevated to the upper parts, then dry that in the lowest place that is in it so that the arm runs inside, because when the arm is shortened in the pre-ponderance of the sinew, the flesh is engendered in it.
And if it is not possible for you to dry the sinew inside the environment of the lowest bone according to your will, then pierce it so that you prepare the limb with a preparation by which the arm runs lightly according to what is at your apparel and that no cause of the arm be retained in it.
But that which is on the orifice of the sinew, which you remove every hour so that that which is adjusted in it of the arm may escape. And so that you know if that which runs from it of the arm is much or little, or is digested, or is not digested.
And thus you consider the place of that sinew, if in it the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess in it.
And as your medication is prolonged in this manner, and you see the matter that is thrown over the orifice of the sinew already adheres, or appropriates adhesion, then the most you untie it or the third day, and when you untie the plaister, then change the cloth for another and renew the wash.
But if from the sinew a little space appears a subtle virus, then do not despair of its adhesion, because the healing of it approaches, because some men in whom a late generation of flesh in the wounds, and of those it is done the contrary of it.
And if from the sinew after many days a digested arm is emitted, then know that the sinew does not adhere; and if the adhesion of the sinew is delayed and is the prolonged cause, then you adjust in the drying of the medicines, and if the medicines are humid in their substance and in their virtue, they are dried as a diaphynicon wash, when there is in it adjusted superfluity of addition of zegi.
And the last of all which is cured, is that you take of diaphynicon wash and be dissolved in rose oil, and be on it poured a little honey in its substance, and then mix it with it, and use of it.
And already it seems in that action, when there is no arm, diaphynicon wash, honey when it is cooked inside that it be thickened, and use of it; or that you take myrrh and aloe and incense, and grind all and pulverize it over the honey when it is on the fire, and then line it with water over cloth and strengthen it over the sinew; and line it with the honey which you have cooked inside that it be thickened, and pulverize it over cloth and strengthen it.

Of the cure of panariti and  ingrown toenails and  finger incision and section.
Panariti is an abscess that arises from under the nail of the finger or toe, and often arises in the other fingers, and when it is prolonged and its cure is less valued, or is an abscess of an abscess caut, or is corrupted, and throws out pus while it corrodes the roots of the nail, and often corrupts all of it, and often spreads its corruption to the bone until it is a fetid odor, and the extremity of the finger is made numb, and the color of it is made dark.
And therefore when you have that with the water that we have said in the division and do not mix your cure, then know that you should cut with iron all the superfluity that is remaining from the nail and then cauterize the wound with water, because cauterization is very useful in this.
But if the bone is sound and the nail is healthy, and the additions of the nail voids already compress the flesh to the sides of the finger, and they begin to prick it and let it out, then know that you should place a fine ray under the angle of the nail that pricks the flesh, and drive it up and cut it with ease, and place on what remains of the flesh of the medicines comburent and corrosive until it be all removed; and then cure it with washes until it be healed.
But if the corruption has already entered the bone, then know that you should cut the bone and extract it, for no time is it healed that there is in it the corrupted bone.
And if you see the corrosion and corruption going into the said wound, then you cut it in one of the nuts according to how the remembrance of it is pressed, and then take care of it while it is healing.
If the nail is struck or rubbed, and pain is felt in that area, then as you begin to treat the patient, dry the nail with a sharp spatula with a transverse section from top to bottom, and be careful that the section does not reach the flesh that remains under the nail, for you will cause the patient intense pain, and it will lead to the birth of superfluous flesh in the area; and then treat the area with water that soothes the pain.
But this adjusted flesh, which is born in the hands of some men, is very hard, and it is very hard in the bones, or very hard in the nail.
And some of them are born at the root of the joint, or the birth of them in some of the said nuts. But that one that is born in some of the nuts of the finger does not harm, and this one that is born in the joints is very harmful.
And of those that are born fleshy, the section is lighter, and it is that you cut that one, following its root with a broad spatula.
But of that one that is born at the root of the joint, the cure is difficult; and therefore be careful of the abscess of it.
But in that one that is born in the finger, when you cut it at the beginning, the flesh of it with a round incision inside the bone, and then saw it with one of those saws convenient to water, and then take care of it while it is healing.
But consolidation which happens to the fingers, either between their many movements or by birth of the man who is born so, or by consolidation of plague or by burning of fire, or by similar things, then you must remove that consolidation while the fingers return to their natural form.
And place between their cloths of the infused in olive oil rubbed so that they are not consolidated lightly, and separate between those, or place between those a lamina of thin lead while it is consolidated according to what you command.
And similarly if consolidation happens in some fingers with the palm, then you cut that consolidation according to what is prepared and convenient to the figure of the limb.
Of incisions of vices, they are varicose.
Vices are varicose, and they are veins that are thick and full of melancholic superfluity, which come in motion in the limbs of the body, and the major arrival of them in the legs, and most in the legs of the travelers and the laborers and the carriers.
Therefore, you must administer purgation of the body of black bile some times with strong expulsion, and then bleed the patient from the basilica vein.
But the cure of them with iron is according to two manners: one is that it is incised and that the black blood is thrown out, and the other manner is that the vein is elevated and all of it is extracted.
The incision of it is according to this manner: embroca at the beginning the leg with lukewarm water so that the thick blood is resolved, which is feculent of the leg, and then strengthen the leg of the patient to the most sovereign part of the groin into the part below the knee with a bandage, and then cut the vein in a place, or in two, or in three with a wide incision, and then elevate the black blood with your hand from the part below the leg into above, and from below upwards, until the quantity of blood that you want and that you see is enough, and which will take the virtue of the ailment.
And then cover it, and command him to abstain from the foods that generate black bile.
And repeat the cure by phlebotomy when the veins are full and that night to the patient.
But the elevation of them is according to this manner: you that raise the leg of the patient, if in it there are movements, and then put it in a bath and embroca the leg of it with lukewarm water until it reddens and the veins are exuberant; or that it be exercised by strong exercise, if the bath is not present to you, until the limb be scalded.
And then cut the vein in the right of the vein by incision in the long or in the back of it of the knee, or in the lowest part of it of the ankle.
And then open the vein with pincers and scrape the vein from all parts until it appears to the feeling, and it is of the appearance of it that sometimes that rug is declining to blackness.
And therefore, when you evacuate and from the vein you see that white which is cord.
And then you put below it the ray until it is elevated and is thrown from the vein, and suspend it with an onion or a lion.
And then cut another incision near that incision for three fingers, and then scrape the vein from the part below the vein until it appears.
And then elevate that and cut that in the back incision of the ankle, and then extract that and elevate it until it is extracted through the second incision, and then extract that from the incision that is above it.
And do this until you extract that from the incision that is most sovereign or most high of all the incisions, until all is extracted; and then cut that.
And if it does not obey you to extract and elevate, then introduce a needle with a strong double thread and tie it there and extract it, or introduce it behind it the ray and roll your hand to all parts within which it is thrown. And be careful that it is not cut; for if it is broken, it is made difficult for you to elevate that part and it has come upon the patient for that harm.
And when that whole thing is thrown out, then place over the place of the plague wool soaked in wine and oil rubbed and oil unrubbed, and cure that within which it is healed.
And if the gut is contracted having crookedness in which it is wrapped in the parts, and it is not according to straightness according to what we have said, then cover what you do on that to all parts of its crookedness and to the places of its wrapping, and then suspend that with hooks until you elevate that whole thing.
And guard yourself that your section does not cut the vein and that you do not plague that, for it is difficult for you to elevate that; and serve your prudence in that.

On the section for the ailment of nafir.
This ailment is named in our land nafir, and it is the pain which comes in certain limbs, and then is changed from limb to limb.
And I have already seen that as I will tell you. I was called to a sick woman in a village, and uncovered her arm and saw a small inflation in the vein of the arm, and because it was warm for an hour, I saw that inflation go as if a worm was pushing it to this, but more lightly than it should be, as if it were living silver when it runs from place to place.
And then it went to the pain of that place and it felt in the muscle, and then it stayed there for an hour.
And then it moved to the other side of the body until it reached the other arm.
And then I recommended to her that she should roll herself over her whole body as I saw; and it was too marvelous of the permutation of it and the velocity from limb to limb. And I had already seen that before in my own limbs in that manner, however, I have seen many who suffer pain being changed from limb to limb. But I did not see that in the limbs as in the woman.
And I did not think that it was anything but that because the woman was old, or of dry body and uncovered veins, and in this appearance, that windiness was perceived.
And it is necessary that it does not appear according to this retro-cure in those who are delicate and with moist bodies of well-covered veins.
And as you want the cure of it, and the patient feels that pain, then it is not to you apparent at the temple as we have said, then you tighten over it and leave it lightly and squeeze over it until that windiness is contracted, and cauterize the place.
But if you do not see it in your own temples, then you cure it with shaking of the body and with what you expel windiness, and charms those with fetid pills and pills of serapi and similar things.
On the extraction of arrows.
Arrows are diversified according to the species, and according to the places of the body in which they strike, for their diversity is that of those that have large points, and small, and concave, and blunt, so they are solid; and of those that have three angles, and of those that have tongues; and of those that have shafts.
And of the signs of the head is when it strikes there an arrow, and it pierces the bone, and it is issued from the cyphasis which is above the brain, for it accedes through it soda vehement, and scotomia, and vertigo, and roaring in the limbs, and inflammation and roaring of the tongue, and spasm and permutation of understanding and vomiting of bile, and very much the word is absconded and the voice is destroyed, and it is issued from the place of the wound a white humidity resembling dust, and eyes of it resembling the liquidity of the flesh.
And therefore if these signs appear to you, then you abstain from the cure and the extraction of the arrow, if it is not outside.
But the signs of the arrow when it strikes the heart, are that it is near the left nipple, and felt with that which it is fixed in hard cause, and it is not a void cause; and very much the movement of the arrow is similar to the movement of the pulse, and running of the wound black blood, and it feels that cold of the extremities, and sweat cold, and syncope; and therefore know that death descends all through.
And the signs when the arrow has wounded the lung are so much blood spume from the wound, and the vessels that are near the neck are apoplectic, and the color of the patient is changed, and expiries great spirit, and demands traction of cold air.
And if it strikes the arrow in the ligament which is in the foot, and the pain then is near the small of the back, and it is made the ale great with vehement pain and with sigh, and it is not bad all the limbs of the muscles.
And if it strikes the arrow in the stomach, then very much eyes of the wound food any undigested.
And if it strikes the arrow in the belly, and it is fixed in it, eyes some wound of the wound, or the cloth, or the intestine which is dislocated, and there is no hope in the cure of it extraction of the arrow.
And if the arrow enters the bladder, and urine is expelled outside, and something is processed from it to the outside parts, and there is a lot of pain on the patient, then you know that it is mortal.
May the other members, as is the face, the neck, the throat, and the shoulders and arms, and the vertebrae of the back, and the clavicle, and the hip, and the leg and their likenesses of the limbs, be saved according to the greatest dispositions when the arrow does not hit a vein or artery and is not a venomous arrow.
And I recount this to you that I have seen of the being of these arrows, so that you signify by this about your cure.
The cause is, because in a man a shaft pierced the lacrimal of his eye at the root of his nose, and you extracted that from the other part, leaving the gray of the auricle of his eye, and he is healed, and it did not harm the eye.
And I extracted another arrow from a Jew who was shot in the gray of his eye, leaving the eyelid, and the arrow was already hidden and could not be obtained from it except for a small extremity with which it adhered to its shaft, and it was a large arrow of the sharp arrows of the Turks, with a lion's head in which there were no auriculas.
And the Jew healed, and it did not harm his eye at all.
And I extracted another arrow from a Christian man which was lodged in the throat, and it was an Arabic arrow, and that is the one that has auriculas; and therefore I incised upon it between two guides, and it was already submerged in his throat; and therefore I subtly worked with it, and then extracted it, and the Christian healed.
And I extracted another arrow from a man who was shot in his belly, and I thought he would die from it; and therefore, since forty days had passed and nothing had changed about him from his dispositions, I incised upon the arrow and worked with it, and he healed, and it did not harm him at all.
And I saw another man in whom an arrow pierced his back, and the wound was consolidated on him, and since it had been four years, he pulled the arrow out at the root of his thigh.
And I saw a woman to whom an arrow pierced her belly, and the wound was consolidated within her, and it had not changed in her dispositions in any way, and the woman did not suffer any harm in any of her natural operations.
And I saw another man to whom an arrow pierced his face and the wound was consolidated, and he removed the arrow, not finding much pain, and many likenesses to this.
And I extracted the arrow from the man of the prince of the king who was shot in the middle of his nose and had already declined to the right side a little, and the whole arrow was hidden.
And I was called to his cure about three days after the shooting of the arrow.
And then I examined the wound of the arrow very carefully; and then I inquired about it with a subtle touch, and I did not feel it; but I felt a prick below the right auricle, and therefore I suspected that that prick was because of the extremity of the arrow.
And I plastered the place with a plaster which has attractive and digestive virtue, confessing to myself that the place was to be plastered so that it would appear to me the place of the arrow, so that it would dry over it.
And it did not harm the place significantly that the arrow had reached that place; and I continued with the plaster on it for many days and it did not harm at all; and the wound was consolidated meanwhile, and he removed the pain of the extraction of it for a space of many days until one day he felt the arrow inside his nose and recounted this to me.
And then I placed on the wound medicine acute corrosive for many days until it opened, and with the touch I felt it, and examined the extremity of the arrow subtly, which adhered to the shaft.
And then I adjusted it in the appearance of the wound by that acute medicine until it appeared to me visibly the extremity of the arrow, and it passed to me time with that for the space of time within four months.
And then, because the wound was amplified, and it was possible for me to intervene with forceps in it, and remove it, I did not cease to subtly work and engineer on it with ingenious ways, until one day I began to hang it with forceps skillfully made, according to how they will come in the end of the chapter, until I extracted it; and then I restored that wound.
And some physicians judged that the cartilage of the nose was not restored, and I restored it and the wound was consolidated, and the patient healed completely, and he did not suffer in any way.
And I recount to you the quality of the extraction of some arrows so that you pause this rule and signification about what I have not said, because the parts of this art and the definitions of it are not comprehended by the narration nor do those comprehend it in the book.

Of phlebotomy of the veins.

Of suction and the qualities of using them.
Suctions are of horns, or of glass, or of wood.
And suction is done in two ways: one of them is with scarification and extraction of blood, and the other is suction without scarification.
And this suction that is without scarification is in two ways, whether it is with fire or without fire.
And to the suctions that are administered with scarification and extraction of blood there are fourteen locations of the body, of which one in which suctions are placed is the occiput, and it is the back part of the head; and the middle place of the two parts of the neck together; and suctions of the chin below the jawbone; and suctions of the two scapulae; and suctions of the hypochondrium, and it is above the end of the rib; and suctions of the two flanks, and they are of two sides; and suctions of the two armpits; and suctions of the two groins.
And suction does not extract the blood but from the small veins scattered in the flesh, and therefore it does not capture the virtue through those, as it is done by phlebotomy; nor is it advisable that suction be done with fire or without fire in any illness caused by repletion until the whole body is evacuated.
But if necessity provokes suction for illness or for continuity, we administer it at all times at the beginning of the month and at the end of it, and in the middle of it and at any time that is.
And therefore when you see in any of those causes, and properly if it is in the third or middle of the month, then command that suction be done more than it has passed from two or three hours of the day.
And the benefit of suction of the neck is that when that confers gravity to the head and to that which is effused to the eyes; but it is advisable that that be done after the evacuation of the whole body.
And this suction is in the place of phlebotomy of the cephalic.
And it is not light that use of it that which is of phlegmatic complexion, or in which is catarrh, because it gives to that great harm.
And for that reason it is not advisable to use it in the old people, and in the heads of whom are phlegmatic illnesses.
But to him who upon that is continuing upon it is done oblivion; and for that reason it is advisable that you command the suction-maker to place his hand a little with the suction at the parts behind, fearing the generation of oblivion.
But suction of the ankle is in the place of phlebotomy of the vena fusca and basilica: and for that reason it confers to asthma, and to the constriction of the ale and to the scissura of the sturment of ale, and to cough, and to repletion.
And it is advisable that the suction of the ankle be pulled a little, because if it is placed behind, it engenders weakness in the body and in the stomach.
And the suction of the alhagdahan confers to the pains accidental in the head and to ophthalmia, and migraine, and prefoci, and pains in the roots of the teeth; and it is in the place of phlebotomy of the basilica.
And it is advisable that you command the suction-maker that he not press his hand with scarification so that he does not pierce the artery and that a flux of blood does not occur.
And suction below the chin confers to alcohol in the mouth, and to corruption of the gums, and appearances to them of the illnesses that are in the mouth, and stand in the place of phlebotomy of aliheric that is in the two lips.
But the suction that is done upon the two scapulae confers to caphatan, which is made by repletion of heat.
And the suction of the two parts behind the flanks confers benefit of phlebotomy of three veins, that is of the basilica, fusca and cephalica, because that one attracts the blood of all those veins more slender that are in the flesh, and those veins slender of the other veins more gross until that the attraction reaches the three veins.
And command the suction-maker that he does not too much proceed in scarification, because the place is denuded of flesh, and behind it are nerves and arteries.

And command the bellows to be large and of fire, because the place needs a strong incision; and very fine bellows are used and it is to be scarified with a sharp incision.
But bellows applied to the legs are less effective because they draw blood from the whole body, and they resemble old pains in the chest, stomach, and bladder; and they provoke menstruation, and resemble both labor and childbirth; and they are in the place of phlebotomy of two veins, and they are used for the removal of two cavities.
But they weaken the whole body and cause fainting in many men.
And of the bellows, the use is proper to the bellows of two legs.
And the quality of the position of the bellows is that you place the bellows at the beginning and draw it out with a moderate suction, and do not prolong the position of the bellows, but pause them lightly, and move them gently, and that the humors come to the place by gentle arrival. And do not cease to repeat this and continue until you see the place already reddened and inflated and that the color of the blood appears.
And then you scarify and repeat the suction little by little, and then consider in the disposition of the body.
Because that man who has tender flesh, you must scarify him once and no more, so that the place is not ulcerated.
And command the bellows to amplify the scarification and proceed a little, and temper the suction with facility.
And if in the blood there is thickness, then you must scarify twice, because in the first scarification the way of subtlety to the blood and its fluidity is opened. But in the second, to the scrutiny acquired of the extraction of the thick blood.
And if the blood is very foul, then the third scarification should be made so that the last is achieved.
And finally, when we want to extract the blood little by little or a little, one scarification suffices us.
And if we want to extract a lot of blood, we scarify with many scarifications; and if we knew that the blood was thick, then we must scarify with a pre-existing scarification.
And the term of scarification in which the depth of the incision is only.
And if that one whose flesh is thick, hard, dark, and whose pores are narrow, then the places of the bellows should be anointed more gently, more open, more resolved; if it is in summer, as is oil of aloe or oil of violet, or oil of double almonds, or oil of quince; and if it is in winter, then oil of narcissus, or oil of lily, or oil of chamomile, or of saint, and to those similar.
And if the superfluity is thick, sticky, then the oil should be marigold, or oil of balm, or oil of aloe, or oil of anise, and to those similar.
But if the bellows are of wide pores of tender flesh, then it should be prohibited from oil, and it should be washed with waters or with cold water of salvia, or with quince water, or with water of rosemary, and similar to those.
And one whose blood is of much humidity, washes their bellows with sour wine, or with myrtle and sumac water and similar to those.
And one whose superfluities are thick, washes their bellows with old wine, or with water of hyssop, which is marjoram, or of anise decoction, or of chamomile, and similar to those.
And the bellows should be guarded before bathing; bathing should be administered about an hour or two after, and they should sleep near the bellows.
What is necessary to be regulated before bloodletting?
You must consider at the beginning: if the bellows or the one who is to be bled is choleric and has sharp blood and inflammation, then cold causes should be preferred, such as vinegar, endive, sour wine, lettuce, and licorice, and syrup, and similar.
And pause their meals as much as possible, and meats of well-cooked birds, and foods seasoned with sourness, and similar.
And of one whose complexion is cold, it is necessary to encourage the drinking of syrup of licorice, or syrup of althea, and sumac, and wine very fragrant between veal and lamb; and that he be commanded to use little drinking and eating, and to pause from foods of little and canary, and sparrows and small birds and pigeons.
And that on the day of bloodletting and phlebotomy, the drink should be greater than the food.
And that some men be given to drink in some hours before bloodletting or phlebotomy, a mixture of tyriaca alpharac, or medicine of musk, that is nutmeg, or alcelita, so that the main limbs be comforted and the blood be made subtle; and that they should not take those scalfs.
But the bellows that are scarified should be placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and on the umbilicus, in the places of the joints, and on the side of the hip, because these members do not suffer scarification on themselves.
And it is not sought by those (doctors) but the traction of blood from the limb, just as they place a cupping glass on the nipple in the disease of blood flow from the nose; and they use it so that the cold, viscous air from the limb is dissolved, just as they place it on the belly and the navel; for that thins the limb and softens it and removes the pain as it resolves the air.
And it is placed over the boils when they occur in their opening or pus, for by virtue of the strong traction, the pus is drawn out and the boil is eradicated from its place.
And similarly it is done when it is placed over the liver and spleen, drawing out the air enclosed in those.
And these cupping glasses are administered empty with suction alone; and sometimes they are administered with fire.
And sometimes they are administered full of tepid water in the diseases of the spleen.
And this is because the cupping glass is to be filled and be larger, so it is water poured alone or water in which herbs have been boiled suitable for the purpose.
The form of a cupping glass administered with fire: its orifice width is two fingers, as we have formed it; and the quantity of the resin is the majority of a palm; and it is in the place of it, in the place that is in the circuit, the majority of it, the prick is small according to the quantity that enters it a needle.
It is made of a thin, smooth, citron, with large margins, lion, equal and smooth so that it does not damage the limb of its position upon it.
And in the middle of it a transverse bar of iron or steel, upon which a candle is placed with the fire.
And already this cupping glass is larger than the one we have recounted; and the few less according to the diseases and the state of that one who uses it.
And the cupping glasses of the infants and the emaciated are others than the cupping glasses of the young and of robust bodies.
And the quality of placing this cupping glass with fire on the limb is that it extends the fire with firewood decently in front of a small candle of wax, and places it on the middle of the transverse bar in the middle place of the cupping glass, so that the fire is ignited around the departed place so that it does not burn the body of the patient.
And then it is placed over the limb of the patient, and the finger is on the prick that we have said, until when we have the cupping glasses and do not indicate that we show the finger and that the vapor escapes over that prick, then the cupping glass is dissolved instantly.
And prop (i.e., according to) the fire according to its manner, and repeat that if it is indicated by that.
But in a cupping glass that is administered in the disease of pleurisy, with water, in which there is no transverse bar nor prick, and it is not administered unless it is filled with water, and it is placed over the limb alone.
And this is the form of it: And this cupping glass as much as it is larger, so much the better, because it can receive a large quantity of water.

Many signs of fracture of the bone. And for this it is known fracture of the bone: it is the tortuosity of it, and of that eminence and appearance of it to the touch, and so of it when you compress it with your hand.
